- [Concept dribbling fundamentals youth](concept-dribbling-fundamentals-youth.md) — Core youth basketball dribbling fundamentals — fingertip contact, three body positions (speed/control/change-of-pace), no-look vision, and the ball-as-extension-of-hand principle [S15, Ch.3].
- [Concept youth dribbling fundamentals](concept-youth-dribbling-fundamentals.md) — Core youth basketball dribbling principles — ball position, finger pads, eyes up, change of pace, and the four basic perimeter dribble moves — from S15.
- [Concept front pivot youth](concept-front-pivot-youth.md) — Front pivot mechanics and advantages for youth players — 180° pivot bringing the non-pivot foot between the player and defender, staying close to basket [S15, pp.77].

- [Concept motion offense four rules](concept-motion-offense-four-rules.md) — The four universal motion offense rules taught progressively in youth basketball — read, space, move, and react to the dribble — the foundation of all team offense [S15, pp.119-136].
- [Concept motion offense screening rules](concept-motion-offense-screening-rules.md) — The four core motion offense rules governing cutting, spacing, movement on passes/dribbles, and screening communication [S15, pp.157-161].

- [Concept straight stick shooting](concept-straight-stick-shooting.md) — The straight-stick shooting concept for youth players — wrist, elbow, knee, and toe in one vertical line — the foundational alignment check for all basketball shooting [S15, pp.181-189].
- [Concept rebounding areas youth](concept-rebounding-areas-youth.md) — Primary and secondary rebounding area theory for youth players — where missed shots carom based on arc, and how two players should cover each zone [S15, pp.177-179].
- [Concept post scoring at end of dribble](concept-post-scoring-at-end-of-dribble.md) — The 'scoring at the end of the dribble' framework — when post players pick up the dribble near the basket, they use pump fakes, crossovers, and up-and-under moves to finish despite contact.
- [Concept post defensive coverage types](concept-post-defensive-coverage-types.md) — Complete taxonomy of post defensive coverage types — behind, three-quarter, two-step, one-step (fronting), and full fronting — with ball-position triggers and offensive counter for each.
- [Concept perimeter one on one intelligence](concept-perimeter-one-on-one-intelligence.md) — The 'perimeter one-on-one intelligence' framework — 15-foot motion offense spacing, 3-dribble limit, patience-based decision making, and when to make moves vs. when to read and pass.
- [Concept three step read motion offense](concept-three-step-read-motion-offense.md) — The three-step weak-side read in the motion offense: how off-ball players read help-side defender spacing/alignment to choose the correct cut (V-cut, middle cut, or backdoor).
- [Concept low post fakes moves youth](concept-low-post-fakes-moves-youth.md) — Low-post fakes and moves system for youth/motion offense: drop step, spin, half-spin, up-and-under, and pump fake series — with the 3-second post rule, check-baseline principle, and teaching sequence.
- [Concept defensive ball handler stances](concept-defensive-ball-handler-stances.md) — Three on-ball defensive stances for guarding a live-ball offensive player — front-foot-to-pivot-foot, front-foot-to-free-foot, and parallel — each eliminating two of the attacker's three options [S15, pp.266-270].
- [Concept ball you man flat triangle](concept-ball-you-man-flat-triangle.md) — The ball-you-man principle and flat-triangle positioning: help-side defenders position 2/3 from the ball and 1/3 from their assignment, one step off the line between them, using peripheral vision to see both [S15, pp.274-275].
- [Concept individual defensive movement](concept-individual-defensive-movement.md) — Complete individual defensive movement framework for youth basketball: front-foot-to-pivot-foot stance, four foundational steps (advance, retreat, swing, slide), overplay, and help-side duties [S15, pp.283-296]
- [Concept man to man rotation rules](concept-man-to-man-rotation-rules.md) — Man-to-man rotation rules for help-side defense — the two-line system determining who stops the ball vs who covers the basket on a breakaway drive [S15, pp.298-299].
- [Concept team defensive movement principles](concept-team-defensive-movement-principles.md) — Team defensive movement principles from Ch.17 of Youth Basketball Drills — ball-side denial, help-side positioning, cutting/screening defense, and the ball-you-man framework for all five defenders [S15, p.303].
- [Concept team defensive stunts](concept-team-defensive-stunts.md) — Youth team defensive stunts framework — four layered pressure tools (run-and-jump, run-and-trap, trap the dribble, trap the pass) for forcing turnovers or disrupting offensive rhythm, plus channeling as the enabling skill [S15, Ch.19].

- [Concept shooting off the move](concept-shooting-off-the-move.md) — Footwork and handwork principles for shooting off a dribble or cut — inside heel plant, free-foot swing, last-dribble power, and lateral balance for consistent pull-up accuracy.
- [Concept post player getting open](concept-post-player-getting-open.md) — Footwork-based system for offensive post players to get open against aggressive defenders — V-cuts, rip/scrape moves, swim moves, and contact-reverse pivot — the 'battle of the feet' framework from S6 Ch.4.
- [Concept post spin screen](concept-post-spin-screen.md) — The spin screen (lane exchange back screen): two-post action where 02 blindsides X5 on a duck-in cut, forcing a size mismatch switch or a free post catch — detailed footwork.
- [Concept post receiving footwork](concept-post-receiving-footwork.md) — Post player catch fundamentals: two-foot hop, chin the ball, look over high shoulder, read defender and double-teams — the universal starting point for all post moves.
- [Concept post front outside pivot](concept-post-front-outside-pivot.md) — Front outside pivot (and square-up) post move: when the defender cannot be read by feel, use an away-from-basket front pivot to square up facing the defender and basket, preserving the live dribble.
- [Concept sikma inside pivot](concept-sikma-inside-pivot.md) — The Sikma inside pivot (and square-up): a 180° reverse pivot toward the basket and defender that squares the post player up to face the basket — named for an elite post player — creates separation while facing up.
- [Concept defensive box out footwork](concept-defensive-box-out-footwork.md) — Defensive box-out pivot system from S6: front pivot for on-ball defenders boxing out the shooter; reverse pivot for all off-ball defenders — with body position, elbow cues, and short choppy steps.
- [Concept offensive rebounding techniques](concept-offensive-rebounding-techniques.md) — Three pivot-based techniques for offensive players to beat defensive box-outs: butt-to-butt reverse spin, front crossover swim move, and step-back read — from S6 Chapter 5.
- [Concept outlet pass pivot](concept-outlet-pass-pivot.md) — Footwork and pivot mechanics for the defensive rebounder's outlet pass and the outlet receiver's catch — front pivot away from pressure, chin the ball, and attack the frontcourt safely. [S6 Ch.5]
- [Concept flex veer option](concept-flex-veer-option.md) — The flex veer option: post player ducks in high after setting a back screen when the defense focuses on the baseline cutter — exploiting X5 with a reverse pivot into the free-throw lane.
- [Concept flex bump option](concept-flex-bump-option.md) — The flex bump option: guard (01) physically bumps the shoulder of back screener (04) to communicate a reverse pivot direction and duck-in cut, keeping post players inside and guards outside against switching defenses.
- [Concept pin screen footwork](concept-pin-screen-footwork.md) — Pin screen mechanics from S6: cutter footwork (scrape, 180° front pivot, triple threat), screener reverse pivot to post-up, and all defensive adjustments (hedge, switch, trail).
- [Whole part whole teaching method](whole-part-whole-teaching-method.md) — The whole-part-whole teaching method from S6: introduce the full concept, walk through it, drill parts progressively, then reassemble in a team/game-speed setting.
- [Concept defensive pivot drills](concept-defensive-pivot-drills.md) — Three foundational on-ball defensive breakdown drills from S6 Ch.7: push-push (mass), push-and-talk (directional maze), and pride (zigzag full-court) — all teaching reverse pivot drop-step mechanics.
- [Concept trapping footwork](concept-trapping-footwork.md) — Pivot footwork for trappers releasing a trap and rotating after the escape pass (S6 Ch.7): reverse pivot off the outside foot, swing inside foot toward escape pass landing spot, and beat the ball to its destination.
- [Concept whole part whole teaching](concept-whole-part-whole-teaching.md) — John Kimble's whole-part-whole teaching method for basketball: introduce the full concept, break into individual skill parts, then return to game-speed full execution.

- [Concept pivoting fundamentals](concept-pivoting-fundamentals.md) — Pivoting as basketball's most undertaught fundamental — its role in all six phases of the game (ball handling, shooting, post play, rebounding, screening, defense) per John Kimble's S6.

- [Concept basket man ball man](concept-basket-man-ball-man.md) — The basket man / ball man defensive transition system: assigning the first two defenders back on a fast break and their specific responsibilities to stop primary and secondary breaks.
- [Concept pivot footwork cutters screeners](concept-pivot-footwork-cutters-screeners.md) — Pivot footwork for pass receivers and screeners off ball screens: inside-heel front pivot to square up, screen-roll reverse pivot mechanics, and dribbler pull-up technique.
- [Concept 1on1 pivoting techniques](concept-1on1-pivoting-techniques.md) — Four-phase 1-on-1 ball-handler pivoting system for passing out of pressure: step-out, rip-through, swing-around, and counter phases — with full footwork and coaching cues.
- [Concept dribbling driving techniques](concept-dribbling-driving-techniques.md) — Footwork principles for attacking defenders off the dribble: blast move vs. defender's lead foot and front crossover move — step north, scrape the shoulder, protect the ball beside the knee.
- [Concept pivoting while trapped](concept-pivoting-while-trapped.md) — How a ball handler uses the three-phase step-out, rip-through, and swing-around pivoting system to pass out of a double-team trap — with the split-the-trap variation when both flanks are covered.
- [Concept shooter pivot fundamentals](concept-shooter-pivot-fundamentals.md) — Three pivot methods for shooters plus the feet-and-hands-ready principle — the foundational footwork framework enabling quick, low-pressure shot releases from S6.
- [Concept shooter pivots off screens](concept-shooter-pivots-off-screens.md) — How shooters apply inside-foot heel pivots when cutting off down screens, back screens, flare screens, stagger screens, and ball screens to square up and shoot quickly [S6].
- [Concept v cut footwork](concept-v-cut-footwork.md) — The V-cut as a multi-step deceptive off-ball move — not just a jab step — using the inside foot to plant, change direction, and exploit screens for open shots [S6].
- [Concept pivoting offense](concept-pivoting-offense.md) — The foundational role of pivoting in all offensive basketball actions — why pivoting precedes passing and dribbling and is the most critical skill for avoiding turnovers [S6].
- [Concept shooting off the move footwork](concept-shooting-off-the-move-footwork.md) — Complete footwork mechanics for shooting off the dribble or off a cut — inside heel pivot, free foot swing, last-dribble technique, and bilateral training principles.
- [Concept offensive post footwork](concept-offensive-post-footwork.md) — Complete footwork framework for the offensive post player: getting open, the battle of the feet, V-cut reads, the rip move, swim move, contact and reverse pivot, and spin screen — S6 Ch.4.
- [Concept post v cut get open](concept-post-v-cut-get-open.md) — Post player V-cut system for getting open: how to read defensive position and use a 2-3 step misdirection cut with a front crossover pivot and rip or swim arm action to receive the ball inside.
- [Concept post contact reverse pivot](concept-post-contact-reverse-pivot.md) — The contact and reverse pivot move for offensive post players — stepping the contact foot between the defender's feet and reverse-pivoting to seal the baseline side for a duck-in entry pass.
- [Concept post spin screen move](concept-post-spin-screen-move.md) — The spin screen move — a two-player interior back screen by a weakside teammate that frees the ballside post player to receive the ball in the lane when individual getting-open moves are stopped.
- [Concept spin screen post action](concept-spin-screen-post-action.md) — The spin screen two-man post action: duck-in cut triggers a blind back screen (small-on-big) from the weak-side post, creating mismatches and dual scoring threats.
- [Concept post catch mechanics](concept-post-catch-mechanics.md) — Complete post catch mechanics: two-foot hop at catch, chinning the ball, reading over the high shoulder, and elbow-out ball protection before initiating any post move.
- [Concept show and go opposite drop step](concept-show-and-go-opposite-drop-step.md) — The show-and-go-opposite drop-step post move: read the defender's position, show the ball as bait, reverse-pivot drop-step to the open side, power dribble, and finish at 45° off the glass.
- [Concept olajuwon whirl move](concept-olajuwon-whirl-move.md) — The Olajuwon whirl post move: front-pivot 180° away from the defender to face the basket, sealing with the chest/side, power-dribble advance, and 45° finish off the glass.
- [Concept post pivot square up](concept-post-pivot-square-up.md) — Two post pivot/square-up techniques for when the defender's position cannot be read: the Front Outside Pivot and the Sikma Inside Pivot — both establish a face-up position from which any perimeter-like attack can be launched.
- [Concept spin screen footwork](concept-spin-screen-footwork.md) — The spin screen: post-to-post interior back screen where the cutter fakes high, reverse pivots off the screen, and crosses the lane — with detailed pivot mechanics for both screener and cutter.
- [Concept flex back screen footwork](concept-flex-back-screen-footwork.md) — Flex back screen footwork mechanics: screener's front pivot after setting the screen, flare screen sequence, cutter's V-cut setup, and the three-threat scoring system that makes this action hard to defend.
- [Concept screen the screener footwork](concept-screen-the-screener-footwork.md) — Screen-the-screener action off the flex offense: footwork for the original screener (04) to get open off a down screen and quickly catch-and-shoot before the defense can recover.
- [Concept flex veer option footwork](concept-flex-veer-option-footwork.md) — The veer option off the flex back screen: screener (05) ducks into the lane high after the cutter scrapes low, exploiting defensive over-help with a reverse pivot post-up in the free throw lane.
- [Concept flex bump option footwork](concept-flex-bump-option-footwork.md) — The flex bump option: the guard (01) physically bumps the post screener (04) to signal a role switch — 04 reverse pivots into the lane and 01 replaces himself on the perimeter, exploiting switching defenses.
- [Concept high-post rub off screen footwork](concept-rub-off-screen-footwork.md) — High-Post rub-off screen at the high-post elbow: screener (04) sets a stationary back screen for the PG (01) cutting to the low post, with three post-screen options and detailed butt-screen pivot mechanics.
- [Concept high-post bump footwork](concept-high-post-bump-footwork.md) — The High-Post bump: guard (01) bumps the high-post screener (04) to redirect him from the High-Post cut to a ballside low-post flash, while 01 replaces at the top — counter to switching defense on the High-Post rub-off.
- [Concept stagger screen footwork](concept-stagger-screen-footwork.md) — Stagger screen footwork from S6: the first screener's reverse pivot after the cutter scrapes off, using the second screener as a brush screen, creating two simultaneous scoring threats off the staggered action.
- [Concept pin screen](concept-pin-screen.md) — The pin screen — off-ball screen that pins a defender to free a perimeter cutter, with screener reverse-pivot post-up as the secondary scoring threat.
- [Concept on ball defensive pivots](concept-on-ball-defensive-pivots.md) — On-ball defensive pivot footwork: the drop-and-swing step, push-push method, and four basic ball-defender movements for staying in front of dribble penetration.
- [Concept defensive footwork breakdown drills](concept-defensive-footwork-breakdown-drills.md) — Three foundational defensive footwork breakdown drills from S6 Ch.7: push-push (mass), push-and-talk (maze), and pride/zigzag (full-court) — all training the drop-and-swing pivot system.
- [Concept trapping footwork pivots](concept-trapping-footwork-pivots.md) — Pivoting footwork for trappers after an escape pass — reverse pivot off the outside foot to pursue the new ball location and beat the pass to its landing spot.
- [Concept defensive rebounding footwork](concept-defensive-rebounding-footwork.md) — Defensive rebounding pivot footwork: on-ball defender uses a front pivot; all four off-ball defenders use reverse pivots to execute box-outs on every missed shot.

- [Face guard press](face-guard-press.md) — The full-court face-guard man-to-man press: body-to-body denial on all receivers, inbounds trap, and rover variation to force long passes and create interceptions.
- [Run and jump defense](run-and-jump-defense.md) — The run-and-jump defensive tactic: nearest open defender sprints to jump the dribbler, forcing a hurried decision while the original ball defender rotates to the free man.
- [Concept defensive philosophy herb brown](concept-defensive-philosophy-herb-brown.md) — Herb Brown's overall defensive philosophy: match personnel to system, be consistent, and use defense as the great equalizer when offense fails.
- [Concept basketball warmup protocol](concept-basketball-warmup-protocol.md) — Arnie Kander's (pro team) complete standing basketball warm-up protocol: starting position, 18-movement basic routine, and 13-drill running program — all sport-specific, no floor stretches.
- [Basketball glossary defensive terms](basketball-glossary-defensive-terms.md) — Herb Brown's comprehensive defensive terminology glossary — ball-you-man, belly up, blitz, bump, close out, cover down, deny, digging, and more.
- [Basketball glossary offensive terms](basketball-glossary-offensive-terms.md) — Herb Brown's comprehensive offensive basketball terminology glossary — sets, cuts, screens, passes, and tactical signals from Let's Talk Defense.
- [Practice with a purpose](practice-with-a-purpose.md) — Shawn Nelson's practice philosophy: game-speed purposeful repetition as the foundational habit for developing offensive skills.
- [Concept rip step workout series](concept-rip-step-workout-series.md) — The Rip Step Workout Series — a structured progressive training system (Workouts #2-5 through #2-18) building all four rip step finishing options with escalating volume and bilateral practice.
- [Concept shot fake stride stop](concept-shot-fake-stride-stop.md) — The shot fake into stride stop: how to use a shot fake to freeze a defender then drive past with 1 or 2 dribbles into a balanced stride stop for a pull-up jumper.
- [Concept shot fake step through](concept-shot-fake-step-through.md) — The shot fake into stride stop with step-through counter: when the defender jumps the shot fake, step under/through their body for a higher-percentage layup or contact shot.
- [Concept shot fake big hop](concept-shot-fake-big-hop.md) — The shot fake into big hop: freeze the defender with a fake, then attack off 1-2 dribbles and gather into a wide two-foot jump stop (big hop) for an explosive pull-up jumper.
- [Concept shot fake hop back](concept-shot-fake-hop-back.md) — The shot fake into hop back: fake drives the defender forward, then the ball handler hops backward to create shooting space for an open three-pointer or midrange jumper.
- [Concept shot fake hop back roll out](concept-shot-fake-hop-back-roll-out.md) — The shot fake hop back to roll-out dribble: fake drives the defender forward, hop back creates space, then a roll-out dribble attacks the recovering defender's new position.
- [Concept shot fake hop back crossover](concept-shot-fake-hop-back-crossover.md) — The shot fake hop back to crossover dribble: most advanced version of the hop-back series — after hopping back and seeing the defender recover, a crossover dribble attacks the opposite direction.
- [Concept shot fake workout series](concept-shot-fake-workout-series.md) — The systematic shot-fake workout series from S3: progressive volume structure, FT interleaving, and the full hierarchy of shot-fake moves from stride stop through hop-back crossover.
- [Concept combination live ball moves](concept-combination-live-ball-moves.md) — Combination live-ball moves: chaining multiple 1-on-1 attack moves (rip step, shot fake, hop-back, crossover) to put defenders off-balance and create scoring opportunities.
- [Concept hop back crossover combo](concept-hop-back-crossover-combo.md) — Combination live-ball move: hop-back dribble into a crossover dribble — creating separation and attacking the defense off the dribble.
- [Concept shooting off screens s3](concept-shooting-off-screens-s3.md) — Complete framework for shooting off screens from S3: cutter rules (read, verbalize, shoulder-to-shoulder), screener rules, and curl/fill/fade decision-making.
- [Concept reading defender off screen](concept-reading-defender-off-screen.md) — How to read a defender's position coming off a screen and choose the correct attack: fade (baseline), fill (wing), or curl (middle).
- [Concept skills conditioning](concept-skills-conditioning.md) — Skills conditioning philosophy: forcing athletes to execute offensive skills (shooting, dribbling, scoring) while fatigued — the bridge between practice reps and game performance.
- [Concept shots a day club](concept-shots-a-day-club.md) — The Shots-a-Day Club framework: a scalable high-volume daily shooting system (300–500+ shots) for dedicated players building work ethic and shot consistency.
- [Concept off season shooting challenge](concept-off-season-shooting-challenge.md) — Framework for off-season shooting challenges (10k–20k game shots, 1k–4k three-pointers made) — scalable goal-based systems to develop work ethic and shot volume accountability.
- [Concept individual shooting workout design](concept-individual-shooting-workout-design.md) — Principles for designing individual shooting workouts: alternating spot shots with free throws, make-based vs. attempt-based goals, favorite vs. weakest spots, and escalating volume progressions.
- [Offensive skill development practice philosophy](offensive-skill-development-practice-philosophy.md) — Shawn Nelson's practice philosophy: purposeful game-speed repetition, motivation, goal-setting, and progress tracking as the foundation for offensive skill development.
- [Concept rip step](concept-rip-step.md) — The rip step live-ball move: mechanics, pivot foot establishment, directional reads, and all scoring opportunities off the rip — Nelson's foundational offensive concept.
- [Concept shot fake step fake](concept-shot-fake-step-fake.md) — Shot fake/step fake live-ball move: how to execute, scoring opportunities off the fake, and fundamental principles.
- [Concept live ball combination moves](concept-live-ball-combination-moves.md) — Live-ball combination offensive moves: stride stop, step-through, big hop, hop back, and roll-out — the full framework for creating shots off the dribble.
- [Concept live ball workout system](concept-live-ball-workout-system.md) — The structured live-ball workout system: how to organize combo shooting sessions using volume progressions (80→120→240 shots), bilateral training, and embedded FT clusters.
- [Concept shooting off a screen](concept-shooting-off-a-screen.md) — Complete framework for shooting off screens — cutter and screener responsibilities, curl/fill/fade reads, and the communication system between teammates.
- [Concept dribble fade shot](concept-dribble-fade-shot.md) — The dribble fade — reading a high-angle closeout off a screen and attacking the baseline with a live dribble for any scoring opportunity.
- [Concept dribble fill shot](concept-dribble-fill-shot.md) — The dribble fill — reading a low/trailing closeout off a screen and attacking the middle of the paint with a live dribble for any scoring opportunity.
- [Concept fill shot off screen](concept-fill-shot-off-screen.md) — The fill shot — a stationary catch-and-shoot on the wing after setting up a screen, taken 15–20 feet from the basket when the defender goes under or is beaten.
- [Concept curl shot off screen](concept-curl-shot-off-screen.md) — The curl shot — cutter curls tightly off a screen to the elbow area (10–15 ft) and shoots when the defender is on the high side or trailing.
- [Concept dribble curl shot](concept-dribble-curl-shot.md) — The dribble curl — defender trails directly behind the cutter on a curl cut, so the cutter continues into the paint with a dribble curl attack for any scoring opportunity.
- [Concept off screen shot selection framework](concept-off-screen-shot-selection-framework.md) — The complete defender-read framework for off-screen shot selection: fade, fill, curl, dribble fade, dribble fill, and dribble curl — based on defensive coverage angle.

- [Skill vs athleticism](skill-vs-athleticism.md) — The critical distinction between basketball skill (e.g., jump shooting) and athleticism (e.g., jumping ability) — training improves one, practice improves the other.

- [Shooting hand grip](shooting-hand-grip.md) — How to grip the basketball correctly: fingertips/fingerpads only, L-shaped arm, daylight check, and seaming for backspin.
- [Shooting elbow alignment](shooting-elbow-alignment.md) — Elbow is the single most important shooting component: must be tucked under the ball, above the shooting foot, in L-position to ensure a straight shot.
- [Shooting balance hand](shooting-balance-hand.md) — The balance hand's role is to support and lift the ball only — never to guide or shoot — with correct T-thumb placement on the side of the ball.
- [Shooting target focus](shooting-target-focus.md) — Shooters must always target the center of the basket — the one consistent aiming point from any court location — except on bank shots.
- [Shot ready position](shot-ready-position.md) — Being shot ready means pre-setting the shooting hand and elbow in L-position BEFORE receiving a pass so the player only needs to catch and lift.
- [Shooting technique fundamentals](shooting-technique-fundamentals.md) — Overview of complete shooting mechanics: build the shot from the ground up through stance, grip, elbow, balance hand, target focus, and follow-through.
- [Shooting follow through](shooting-follow-through.md) — Correct follow-through mechanics for basketball shooting: shot line, elbow height, hand position, balance hand, and freeze cue.
- [Free shot technique](free-shot-technique.md) — Complete technique guide for free-throw shooting: stance, grip, routine, mental approach, and follow-through from Basketball Shooting.
- [Midrange jump shot](midrange-jump-shot.md) — Complete guide to midrange jump shot mechanics: why it matters, straight-on technique, stance, shot pocket, one-two step, and receiving the ball.
- [Concept jump shot release and follow through](concept-jump-shot-release-and-follow-through.md) — Proper release timing and frozen follow-through mechanics for midrange and long-range jump shots.

- [Concept midrange jump shot](concept-midrange-jump-shot.md) — Complete midrange jump shot mechanics: one-two step, catch, release, follow-through, and the pull-up variation off the dribble.
- [Concept one two step footwork](concept-one-two-step-footwork.md) — The one-two step catch footwork for jump shots: how to generate power and momentum from the non-shooting foot leading into the shooting foot.
- [Concept three point shot technique](concept-three-point-shot-technique.md) — Complete three-point shot techniques: footwork for straight-on, on-the-move, and off-dribble long-range jump shots, plus game situation tactics.

- [Bank shot](bank-shot.md) — The bank shot — technique, optimal angles/distances, and why it remains a high-percentage scoring weapon at every level.
- [Creating your own shot](creating-your-own-shot.md) — Framework for creating a shot under defensive pressure: dribble with purpose, fakes, reads, and how to be efficient within an offense.
- [Shot fake](shot-fake.md) — The shot fake — technique, footwork, common errors, and practice progressions for creating scoring opportunities against aggressive defenders.
- [Show and go](show-and-go.md) — The show-and-go: shot fake into a drive past a defender, covering strong-side and weak-side reads, arm bar protection, and footwork progressions.
- [Arm bar ball protection](arm-bar-ball-protection.md) — The arm bar technique for protecting the dribble when driving past a defender — L-shape, closed fist, tight to the body.
- [Concept show and go](concept-show-and-go.md) — The show-and-go shot fake move: catch, show the ball, rip to hip, drive past defender — strong-side and weak-side variations.
- [Concept jab step](concept-jab-step.md) — The jab step: a short, quick nonpivot-foot feint at the defender to create a shooting or driving advantage — full series including jab-rise-shoot, jab-jab-jumper, jab-jab-and-go.
- [Concept step back](concept-step-back.md) — The step-back move: using the inside pivot foot to create shooting space against help defenders — weak-side and strong-side variations, plus the step-back-rise-up-and-go counter.
- [Concept combination scoring moves](concept-combination-scoring-moves.md) — Principles for chaining shot fakes, jab steps, and step backs into combination scoring sequences — the mindset and method of a complete one-on-one scorer.
- [Concept shooting off screens](concept-shooting-off-screens.md) — Complete technique for shooting off screens: body-to-body positioning, V-cut setup, inside pivot foot catch, heel-to-toe landing, and defender-reading principles.
- [Concept not open dribble reaction off screen](concept-not-open-dribble-reaction-off-screen.md) — When a defender fights through a screen, the ball receiver must immediately protect the ball with an outside-hand dribble and attack off the dribble.
- [Concept shooting on the move](concept-shooting-on-the-move.md) — Core principles for shooting while moving — inside pivot foot plant, squaring to basket, game-speed practice, and carry-through of technique from footwork to finish.
- [Concept shot charting and evaluation](concept-shot-charting-and-evaluation.md) — System for tracking shooting workouts via shot charts and evaluating shooting mechanics via a structured evaluation form — the shooting specialist's documentation approach.
- [Play selection principles](play-selection-principles.md) — Core principles for selecting and designing plays: formation deception, personnel fit, body language, and keeping playbooks simple.
- [Concept reading screens off ball](concept-reading-screens-off-ball.md) — How off-ball players read their defender on down screens, flare screens, and double screens to choose the best cut.
- [Concept setting screens](concept-setting-screens.md) — Principles for setting legal, effective screens including angle, timing, hold, and hunting the defender.
- [Concept anatomy hip flexor complex](concept-anatomy-hip-flexor-complex.md) — The iliopsoas, rectus femoris, sartorius, and TFL group that drives cutting, driving, and first-step acceleration. Part of the anterior kinetic chain per [S2, p.32].
- [Concept anatomy glute max](concept-anatomy-glute-max.md) — The gluteus maximus as horizontal-propulsion engine for drives, defensive slides, and vertical jumps. Primary muscle trained by the hip thrust per [S2, pp.18-19].
- [Concept anatomy ankle complex](concept-anatomy-ankle-complex.md) — ATFL, CFL, and the ligament-plus-calf system that controls landing, cutting, and pivoting. Ligament-dominant region; proprioceptive instrument that determines injury risk per [S2] Ch.7.
- [Concept anatomy core outer](concept-anatomy-core-outer.md) — The rectus abdominis, obliques, and erector spinae that "produce and resist spinal movement in multiple planes" [S2, p.32]. Anti-rotation and anti-extension training target.

## Drills
- [Drill running outside the lines s15](drill-running-outside-the-lines-s15.md) — Multi-skill warm-up drill: team jogs out-of-bounds perimeter reacting to verbal commands for stops, pivots, fakes, dribble moves, and defensive footwork [S15, pp.4-5]
- [Drill mirror slap s15](drill-mirror-slap-s15.md) — Partner mirroring drill: Player A leads movements (touches, fakes, pivots, defensive steps); Player B mirrors — builds reactive quickness and defensive/offensive footwork [S15, pp.6-7]
- [Drill dribbling off wall s15](drill-dribbling-off-wall-s15.md) — Solo wall dribbling drill: dribble off wall at varying heights and elbow angles, then with individual fingers only — builds fingertip control and ball-handling agility [S15, pp.8-9]
- [Drill lane slide s15](drill-lane-slide-s15.md) — Foul lane defensive slide drill: 3 players slide side-to-side, touching lane lines with outside foot, counted for 30-60 seconds — builds defensive footwork, quickness, and conditioning [S15, pp.10-11]
- [Drill quick hands s15](drill-quick-hands-s15.md) — Defensive quick-hands drill: player in stance deflects coach's live dribble with rapid snake-strike hand action; advanced: 2v1 scramble 1-on-1 after deflection [S15, pp.12-13]
- [Drill quick foot movement s15](drill-quick-foot-movement-s15.md) — Foot-pattern quickness drill using lettered floor positions (A-E): players execute a multi-step hop/jump/180-turn sequence for 25 seconds — builds foot speed, coordination, and pivoting quickness [S15, pp.14-15]
- [Drill agility tip drill s15](drill-agility-tip-drill-s15.md) — Wall-facing jump and 90-degree turn drill: players jump, touch wall, turn 90 degrees on the way down, repeat continuously — builds jump conditioning, agility, and defensive footwork [S15, pp.16]
- [Drill youth basic layup](drill-youth-basic-layup.md) — Basic layup drill (Drill 8) — two-line team drill teaching layup mechanics, bounce/chest passing, and rebounding with beginner/intermediate/advanced progressions for youth players [S15, pp.18-19]
- [Drill youth triple threat position](drill-youth-triple-threat-position.md) — Triple-threat position drill (Drill 9) — V-cut to catch, reverse pivot into triple-threat stance, progressing to fakes, drives, and pull-up jumpers for youth players [S15, pp.20-21]
- [Drill youth post position](drill-youth-post-position.md) — Post position drill (Drill 10) — teaching youth players to establish low-post position against any defender location, receive the entry pass, and execute post moves with progressive live defender reads [S15, pp.22-23]
- [Drill youth rocker step](drill-youth-rocker-step.md) — Rocker step drill (Drill 11) — the four-stage jab step series (jab, jab-pullback, jab-direct drive, jab-crossover) teaching youth players all pre-dribble offensive footwork reads [S15, pp.24-25]
- [Drill youth in and out move](drill-youth-in-and-out-move.md) — In-and-out move drill (Drill 12) — teaching the in-and-out dribble fake to beat a straight-up or same-side-foot defender, complement to the crossover, with dominant then weak hand [S15, pp.26-27]
- [Drill youth crossover move](drill-youth-crossover-move.md) — Crossover move drill (Drill 13) — teaching the crossover dribble to beat an overplaying defender, complement to the in-and-out move, with dominant then weak hand [S15, pp.28-29]
- [Drill youth spin move](drill-youth-spin-move.md) — Spin (reverse) move drill (Drill 14) — teaching the 360-degree reverse pivot dribble move to beat an overplaying or straight-up defender, with counter to the half-spin [S15, pp.30-31]
- [Drill youth half spin move](drill-youth-half-spin-move.md) — Half-spin move drill (Drill 15) — teaching the 90-degree fake spin with immediate reversal to beat a defender expecting the full spin move; counter to the spin move [S15, pp.32-33]
- [Drill youth combination dribbling](drill-youth-combination-dribbling.md) — Combination dribbling moves drill (Drill 16) — chaining rocker step + any dribble move (in-and-out, crossover, spin, half-spin) from a V-cut catch in a rotating court setup [S15, p.34]
- [Drill youth paye drill](drill-youth-paye-drill.md) — Paye Drill (Drill 17) — comprehensive 3-part read-and-react 1-on-1 drill teaching offensive players to read defensive stance, coverage, and overplay and select the correct move before, during, and after the dribble [S15, pp.35-36]
- [Drill paye drill](drill-paye-drill.md) — The Paye Drill — 3-part 1v1 read-and-react system teaching offensive attacks before, during, and after the dribble against all defensive coverages [S15, pp.37-41].
- [Drill fingertip drill](drill-fingertip-drill.md) — Fingertip Drill (Drill #18) — individual 30-second touch drill developing fingertip ball-handling and wrist-flip mechanics for youth basketball players [S15, p.45].
- [Drill standing figure 8 ballhandling](drill-standing-figure-8-ballhandling.md) — Standing Figure 8 (Drill #19) — individual/team 2-minute ball-handling drill passing and dribbling the basketball in a figure-8 pattern around both legs to develop touch and coordination [S15, pp.46-47].
- [Drill figure 8 dribble](drill-figure-8-dribble.md) — Figure 8 Dribble (Drill #20) — individual/team 2-minute dribbling drill running a figure-8 pattern through the legs, advancing from stationary to full-court racing [S15, pp.48-49].
- [Drill side to side dribble](drill-side-to-side-dribble.md) — Side-to-Side Dribble (Drill #21) — individual/team 2-minute drill dribbling the ball front-to-back and side-to-side without watching it, building touch and ambidextrous control [S15, p.50].
- [Drill spider dribble](drill-spider-dribble.md) — Spider Dribble (Drill #22) — individual/team 30-second drill developing touch, hand-eye coordination, and hand quickness through rapid alternating front/back hand taps below the body [S15, p.51].
- [Drill speed dribble youth](drill-speed-dribble-youth.md) — Speed Dribble (Drill #23) — individual/team 1-minute full-court speed dribbling drill with pivot, jump stop, and pass, teaching proper speed-dribbling position and two-ball variations [S15, pp.52-53].
- [Drill control dribble youth](drill-control-dribble-youth.md) — Control Dribble (Drill #24) — individual/team 1-minute full-court control-dribbling drill zigzagging down the floor, building ball-protection position, pivot, and pass skills [S15, pp.54-55].
- [Drill change of pace dribble](drill-change-of-pace-dribble.md) — Change of Pace Dribble (Drill #25) — individual/team 1-minute full-court drill alternating fast and slow dribbles to develop the change-of-pace move and conditioning [S15, pp.56].
- [Drill hesitation dribble s15](drill-hesitation-dribble-s15.md) — Hesitation dribble full-court drill — slow-explode-stop change-of-pace dribble series building ball control and deceptive pace changes [S15, pp.58-59].
- [Drill retreating dribble](drill-retreating-dribble.md) — Retreating dribble full-court drill — backward slide-step dribble escaping traps with 45-degree angle re-attack, bilateral practice, and dual-ball advanced versions [S15, pp.60-61].
- [Drill in and out dribble s15](drill-in-and-out-dribble-s15.md) — In-and-out dribble maneuver full-court drill — fake crossover using a one-handed pull-back dribble with taped boxes marking the move locations, bilateral practice [S15, pp.62-63].
- [Drill crossover dribble s15](drill-crossover-dribble-s15.md) — Crossover dribble maneuver full-court drill — low, quick crossover at taped boxes with head/shoulder fakes and bilateral practice [S15, pp.64-65].
- [Drill spin reverse dribble s15](drill-spin-reverse-dribble-s15.md) — Spin (reverse) dribble maneuver full-court drill — 180° spin at taped boxes, ball control through the turn, and bilateral practice [S15, pp.66-67].
- [Drill half spin dribble s15](drill-half-spin-dribble-s15.md) — Half-spin dribble maneuver full-court drill — incomplete reverse spin that redirects the ball back in the original direction, confusing defenders [S15, pp.68-69].
- [Drill fun cone dribbling](drill-fun-cone-dribbling.md) — Fun cone dribbling drill — haphazard cone maze on a full court where players execute coach-called dribble moves at each cone, beginner through intermediate [S15, p.70].
- [Drill dribble tag s15](drill-dribble-tag-s15.md) — Dribble Tag drill — two players each with a ball in a circle try to slap the other's ball out while maintaining their own dribble; builds ball security and quick hands [S15, p.71].
- [Drill team dribble tag](drill-team-dribble-tag.md) — Team Dribble Tag drill — one 'It' player tries to tag all other dribbling players in a confined space; multiple ball-count variations build footwork, peripheral vision, and ball security [S15, pp.72-73].
- [Drill front pivot s15](drill-front-pivot-s15.md) — Front pivot drill — players dribble full court, jump-stop or stride-stop at the endline, front pivot, and pass back; intermediate version uses coach commands to trigger pivots anywhere on court [S15, pp.76].
- [Drill reverse pivot youth](drill-reverse-pivot-youth.md) — Reverse pivot drill for youth players — dribble to endline, jump-stop, pivot away from defender (180°), pass; individual and team progression [S15, pp.78-79].
- [Drill jump stop youth](drill-jump-stop-youth.md) — Jump stop drill for youth — baseline sprint with coach visual/verbal command to jump-stop; teaches two-foot landing and two-pivot-foot advantage [S15, pp.80-81].
- [Drill stride stop youth](drill-stride-stop-youth.md) — Stride stop (one-two) drill for youth — baseline run with coach command; left foot plants heel-to-toe, right foot swings forward; enables quick jump shot release [S15, pp.82-83].
- [Drill one on two pivoting](drill-one-on-two-pivoting.md) — One-on-two pivoting drill — 1 offensive player uses pivots, step-through, and ball swings to protect the ball against 2 defenders for 30 seconds each [S15, pp.84-85].
- [Drill dribble stop pivot](drill-dribble-stop-pivot.md) — Dribble, Stop, Pivot drill — players dribble on coach signal, stop (jump or stride), pivot (front or reverse), and continue; individual or team, 1 minute [S15, p.86].
- [Drill dribble stop pivot pass cut](drill-dribble-stop-pivot-pass-cut.md) — Dribble, Stop, Pivot, Pass, Cut team drill — pairs dribble, stop, pivot, pass to a V-cutting teammate; integrates all ball-handling and cutting skills [S15, p.87].
- [Drill dribble stop jump shot](drill-dribble-stop-jump-shot.md) — Dribble, Stop, Jump Shot drill — player dribble-drives to a spot, jump-stops or stride-stops, shoots; 5-min individual or team drill with rocker step and live defender progressions [S15, pp.88-89].
- [Drill four corner stopping pivoting](drill-four-corner-stopping-pivoting.md) — Four-Corner Stopping, Pivoting team drill — 4 dribblers attack mid-court simultaneously, stop and pivot, pass to V-cutting out-of-bounds teammates; 8-player rotation, 3 minutes [S15, pp.90-91].
- [Drill two line standing still](drill-two-line-standing-still.md) — Two-Line Standing Still passing drill — partners 15 ft apart practice all pass types stationary; beginner chest/bounce/overhead through advanced baseball passes [S15, pp.94-95].
- [Drill two line moving](drill-two-line-moving.md) — Two-Line Moving passing drill — two diagonal lines exchange passes while moving and rotating; progresses through all pass types in 3 minutes [S15, p.96].
- [Drill two player cutting](drill-two-player-cutting.md) — 2-player motion offense cutting drill (Drill 58) — teaches Rules 1 & 2 of motion offense using cones as defenders; players verbalize cut name and reason [S15, pp.118-119].
- [Drill three player cutting](drill-three-player-cutting.md) — 3-player motion offense cutting drill (Drill 59) — introduces Rules 3 & 4 (every player moves on every pass; cut or fade when dribbler approaches) with verbalization [S15, pp.120-121].
- [Drill defeat help and recover](drill-defeat-help-and-recover.md) — Defeat Help and Recover (Drill 60) — teaches the 3 options for the weak-side offensive player when a help defender closes to stop dribble penetration in the motion offense [S15, pp.122-123].
- [Drill full court cutting](drill-full-court-cutting.md) — Full-court cutting (Drill 61) — continuous full-court passing and cutting drill where passers replace receivers, building passing accuracy, cut timing, and conditioning simultaneously [S15, pp.124-125].
- [Drill two on two pass dribble cut](drill-two-on-two-pass-dribble-cut.md) — 2-on-2 Pass, Dribble, and Cut (Drill 62) — teaches recognition of when to use middle cut, backdoor cut, or V-cut against live defense by running each cut separately then combining [S15, pp.129-131].
- [Drill two on two recognition](drill-two-on-two-recognition.md) — 2-on-2 Recognition (Drill 63) — live 2-on-2 motion offense drill where players must read real defenders and choose the correct cut (middle, backdoor, V-cut, flash pivot) without coaching prompts [S15, pp.132-133].
- [Drill three on three passing cutting spacing](drill-three-on-three-passing-cutting-spacing.md) — 3-on-3 Passing, Cutting, and Spacing without dribbling (Drill 64) — forces sharp cuts and accurate passes by eliminating the dribble; all four motion offense rules applied in live 3-on-3 [S15, pp.134-135].
- [Drill three on three passing cutting dribbling spacing](drill-three-on-three-passing-cutting-dribbling-spacing.md) — 3-on-3 Passing, Cutting, Dribbling, and Spacing (Drill 65) — full integration of all motion offense rules with live dribbling, all dribble moves, rocker steps, and driving options in a live 3-on-3 [S15, pp.136].
- [Drill three player continuous screening](drill-three-player-continuous-screening.md) — Advanced 5-player motion offense drill cycling all screen types (down, back, screen-the-screener, on-ball) continuously — no shooting, 8 minutes [S15, pp.158-161].
- [Drill tip ball off wall pivot](drill-tip-ball-off-wall-pivot.md) — Individual rebounding agility drill: tip ball off wall with alternating hands and complete 360° pivot turns between tips — builds quickness, balance, and offensive tipping technique [S15, p.164].
- [Drill bull in ring rebounding](drill-bull-in-ring-rebounding.md) — Competitive 3-in-the-lane rebounding drill: coach shoots, 3 players battle for caroms using pump fakes, jab step and roll/go, and tipping — first to 3 baskets rotates out [S15, pp.165-167].
- [Drill jab step roll rebounding](drill-jab-step-roll-rebounding.md) — 1-on-1 offensive rebounding drill using jab step and roll / jab step and go vs. defensive boxout — teaches swim move, pivot selection, and rebound angle reading [S15, pp.168-169].
- [Drill one on one blockouts](drill-one-on-one-blockouts.md) — 1-on-1 boxout drill using slide-and-box or immediate boxout vs. jab-step-and-roll/go — defender holds attacker off the ball for 3 seconds [S15, pp.170-171].
- [Drill superman rebounding](drill-superman-rebounding.md) — Individual continuous rebounding conditioning drill: toss ball off backboard to opposite side, slide-step and leap to grab it, repeat — builds second-jump conditioning and airtime [S15, p.172].
- [Drill count slide pivot savvy](drill-count-slide-pivot-savvy.md) — Comprehensive 1v1 rebounding drill from 7 court spots — defender uses immediate or slide-step boxout, offensive rebounder uses jab-step techniques; teaches primary rebounding position rules (savvy) [S15, pp.173-175].
- [Drill two on two rebounding](drill-two-on-two-rebounding.md) — 5-on-5 team drill with two post rebounders and three perimeter passers — integrates low-post moves, defensive boxout techniques, blast-out, and secondary rebounding in one comprehensive drill [S15, p.176].
- [Drill wave good bye](drill-wave-good-bye.md) — Wave Good-Bye shooting drill — whole-team wrist action isolation drill teaching the shooting cup and the wrist-cock → wave-goodbye follow-through sequence [S15, p.182].
- [Drill flip ball drill youth](drill-flip-ball-drill-youth.md) — Flip-Ball Drill — players hold the ball on the shooting hand only and flip it lightly into the air, using the ball's tendency to roll off an improperly aligned hand as instant alignment feedback [S15, p.183].
- [Drill lift extend flip](drill-lift-extend-flip.md) — Lift-Extend-Flip drill — whole-team partner drill teaching the three-phase catapult shooting motion (lift the upper arm, extend the lower arm, flip the wrist) with and without a basketball [S15, pp.184-185].
- [Drill lying down flip ball](drill-lying-down-flip-ball.md) — Lying-Down Flip-Ball Drill — players shoot straight up 8-10 feet while lying on the floor, eliminating all lower-body variables to isolate pure wrist/hand alignment [S15, p.186].
- [Drill flip ball off wall](drill-flip-ball-off-wall.md) — Flip the Ball Off the Wall — wall-based alignment drill where the wall physically locks in straight-stick position (toe, knee, arm, wrist touching the wall) before the player steps back and shoots [S15, pp.187-189].
- [Drill around the world youth](drill-around-the-world-youth.md) — Around the World shooting drill — players must make shots from 7 near-basket spots (Little) and 5 three-point spots (Big) in sequence; competitive team variations included [S15, pp.190-191].
- [Drill no rim shooting](drill-no-rim-shooting.md) — No Rim shooting drill — players must make pure swishes (no rim contact) from 5 angles at progressive distances, building perfect arc and touch [S15, pp.192-193].
- [Drill 21 shooting youth](drill-21-shooting-youth.md) — 21 shooting drill — two teams race to 21 made baskets from the same court location, combining shooting, rebounding, and passing in a competitive team format [S15, p.194].
- [Drill nba shooting drill youth](drill-nba-shooting-drill-youth.md) — NBA Shooting Drill — individual simulation drill with 3PT shot, rebound read (midrange or post finish), and free throw in each possession; track score over 5 possessions per half [S15, p.195].
- [Drill mikan baby hook](drill-mikan-baby-hook.md) — Mikan Drill for Baby Hook — continuous bilateral baby-hook shots from under the basket sliding side-to-side, developing ambidextrous close-range finishing and post conditioning [S15, p.196].
- [Drill post moves passing shooting rebounding](drill-post-moves-passing-shooting-rebounding.md) — Post Moves: Passing-Shooting-Rebounding — comprehensive 4-minute team drill integrating low-post offense, flash pivot cuts, help-side defense, and full offensive/defensive rebounding for the entire team [S15, pp.178-179].
- [Drill baby hook youth](drill-baby-hook-youth.md) — Baby hook shot drill for youth players — left-side-of-basket starting position, back parallel to backboard, single-arm left-hand flip over the rim.
- [Drill rebound pass shoot youth](drill-rebound-pass-shoot-youth.md) — 4-player team shooting drill (30-sec rotations): shooter, passer, two rebounders — integrates shooting, rebounding pivots, cuts, and dribble moves in 4 minutes.
- [Drill quick shooting two players youth](drill-quick-shooting-two-players-youth.md) — Fast-paced 2-player shooting drill — 15-second intervals, 4 floor areas, chest/bounce pass delivery, optional slide-step movement before catch; 2 minutes total.
- [Drill post up mechanics youth](drill-post-up-mechanics-youth.md) — Comprehensive post-up mechanics drill (Drill 96) — teaches posting up, drop step, pump fake, pump-fake crossover, up-and-under, face-up moves, spin, and half-spin in individual or team format.
- [Drill slide step dribble youth](drill-slide-step-dribble-youth.md) — Slide-step dribble drill (Drill 97) — teaches the only safe dribble for post players: one low dribble between the legs with a single lateral slide step, traversing the lane.
- [Drill fronting post youth](drill-fronting-post-youth.md) — Drill 98: post player beats fronting defense using body push and overhead lob — teaches the offensive counter to full fronting with correct arm placement, step, and catch-and-lay mechanics.
- [Drill two step post defense youth](drill-two-step-post-defense-youth.md) — Drill 99: teaches the defensive two-step (and one-step) post coverage technique — defender uses ball-movement cues to slide from three-quarter to fronting position while post player battles for position.
- [Drill roll step post youth](drill-roll-step-post-youth.md) — Drill 100: the offensive 'roll step' counter — post player reads defensive two-step or one-step movement, allows it to complete, then 180° reverse pivots to seal the defender and receive an open pass.
- [Drill three quarter post drill youth](drill-three-quarter-post-drill-youth.md) — Drill 101: teaches three-quarter defensive post coverage and the offensive counter — slide-step battle for the front foot, release to the goal when ball moves to the corner, and using pump fakes to score.
- [Drill high low post passing youth](drill-high-low-post-passing-youth.md) — Drill 102: high-low post passing coordination drill — high-post player (4) reads low-post defender coverage (X5) to select bounce pass, lob overhead pass, or step-and-bounce entry to Player 5.
- [Drill post screening youth](drill-post-screening-youth.md) — Drill 103: two-phase post screening drill — Phase 1: post screens for perimeter players; Phase 2: post-to-post screen with high-low roll-back continuity — teaches calling screens, setting angles, and reading defense.
- [Drill one on one lane drill youth](drill-one-on-one-lane-drill-youth.md) — Drill 104: 1-on-1 perimeter lane drill — offensive player stays in a 15-foot lane, must score in 3 dribbles using a rocker step and dribble move while defender forces direction changes; develops intelligent one-on-one decision-making.
- [Drill 1on1 relief](drill-1on1-relief.md) — 1-on-1 Relief Drill (#105): perimeter 1v1 in a 15-foot lane with a safety-valve passer; player must pass out and re-cut if no shot is created — builds all live-ball moves and cutting reads.
- [Drill 1on1 team](drill-1on1-team.md) — 1-on-1 Team Drill (#106): perimeter live-ball 1v1 with progressive dribble restrictions and pivot-foot alternation — teaches all fakes and moves against a reactive defender.
- [Drill one on one on one on one](drill-one-on-one-on-one-on-one.md) — One-on-One-on-One-on-One (#107): competitive king-of-the-court 1v1 from the head of the key — scorer keeps the ball vs a new defender; first to 10 points wins.
- [Drill 1on1 full court game](drill-1on1-full-court-game.md) — 1-on-1 Full-Court Game (#108): players compete full court using a backboard-toss inbound — winner keeps possession while loser goes to the end of the line; 5-minute format.
- [Drill recovery](drill-recovery.md) — Recovery Drill (#109): coach rolls ball down court at varying speeds; two players race for it — the one who recovers becomes attacker and plays 1v1 back to the basket.
- [Drill one on one on one](drill-one-on-one-on-one.md) — One-on-One-on-One (#110): 3-player competitive 1v1 king-of-the-court format; free-throw determines roles, scorer keeps ball vs new defender, first to 10 points wins — intermediate level.
- [Drill approach and close out](drill-approach-and-close-out.md) — Approach and Close Out Drill (#111): defender rolls ball to attacker and must close out on the live dribbler, bring them under control, then play 1v1 — teaches defensive closeout mechanics.
- [Drill basic three step read](drill-basic-three-step-read.md) — Basic Three-Step Read Drill (#112): offensive player reads help-side defender's spacing/alignment and selects the correct cut (V-cut, middle cut, or backdoor) — the foundational motion offense weak-side drill.
- [Drill penetration drill](drill-penetration-drill.md) — Penetration Drill (#113): 3v3 half-court motion offense drill teaching dribble penetration, help-side positioning, and cut reads off the drive — intermediate motion offense team drill.
- [Drill drop step baseline middle](drill-drop-step-baseline-middle.md) — Drop-Step Baseline/Middle Drill (#114): teaches the two foundational low-post drop steps (baseline power layup, middle baby hook) in a progressive individual format from cutting angle through ball fakes.
- [Drill post spin half spin](drill-post-spin-half-spin.md) — Post Spin and Half-Spin Drill (#115): teaches the spin move and half-spin move as counters to each other off the drop-step middle, creating separation from post defenders — intermediate post move progression.
- [Drill follow the rules motion offense](drill-follow-the-rules-motion-offense.md) — Team motion offense drill: players execute the six rules of motion offense in a prescribed sequential order, with no defense progressing to live 5v5 [S15, p.257].
- [Drill five on five no defense](drill-five-on-five-no-defense.md) — 5-on-5 team offense drill with no defense: players run motion offense freely from multiple formations for 1-minute bursts, progressing to live 5v5 with two-stop requirement [S15, pp.258-259].
- [Drill fence slide](drill-fence-slide.md) — Full-court fence-slide denial drill: defenders practice the denial lateral-slide stance from full-court runs to live 1-on-1 off a V-cut, building off-ball denial footwork [S15, pp.264-265].
- [Drill front foot to pivot foot](drill-front-foot-to-pivot-foot.md) — On-ball defensive footwork drill: X1 places front foot beside attacker's pivot foot, practicing swing step and retreat step responses to jab step, jab-step crossover, and reverse pivot [S15, pp.266-267].
- [Drill front foot to free foot](drill-front-foot-to-free-foot.md) — On-ball defensive overplay drill: X1 places front foot against attacker's free foot with half-body overplay, practicing responses to jab step, jab-step pull-back, jab-step crossover, and reverse pivot [S15, pp.268-270].
- [Drill interception stance](drill-interception-stance.md) — Denial drill where X2 uses fence-slide pressure on the front foot to front-pivot into the passing lane for an interception, or slide-step on a backdoor cut [S15, p.271].
- [Drill close the gap stance](drill-close-the-gap-stance.md) — Help-side drill teaching defenders to switch foot pressure from ball-side (interception) to assignment-side (gap-closing) when the ball handler drives toward their assignment, enabling a charge draw [S15, pp.272-273].
- [Drill help side drill](drill-help-side-drill.md) — 3-player help-side positioning drill: X1 jumps to the ball on a skip pass, establishes a flat triangle in interception stance, and adjusts as both the ball and assignment move [S15, pp.274-275].
- [Drill dual help drill](drill-dual-help-drill.md) — Advanced help-side drill where X1 must help twice in one sequence: deflecting a high-post lob pass AND closing out to draw a charge on a baseline drive [S15, p.276].
- [Drill help the helper](drill-help-the-helper.md) — 3-on-3 half-court drill teaching dual weak-side help mandates: denial, flat triangle, gap closure, rotation, and help-and-recover — intermediate level [S15, pp.278-279]
- [Drill defensive cone](drill-defensive-cone.md) — Competitive 1-on-1 drill where the defender must contain a live dribbler for 3 seconds — using all dribble moves and on-ball defensive tactics — with team count pressure [S15, pp.280-281]
- [Drill defensive step youth](drill-defensive-step-youth.md) — Four-part individual defensive footwork drill teaching the advance step, retreat step, swing step, and slide step — the foundational footwork for on-ball man-to-man defense [S15, pp.285-287]
- [Drill overplay step youth](drill-overplay-step-youth.md) — Full-court overplay slide drill: defender uses nose-on-ball overplay technique to force a live dribbler to change direction at least three times per half-court [S15, pp.288-289]
- [Drill mirror step youth](drill-mirror-step-youth.md) — Parallel baseline mirror drill: defender uses the correct defensive step to counter each attacking move — consolidating advance, retreat, swing, and overplay steps into one reactive sequence [S15, p.290]
- [Drill jump switching youth](drill-jump-switching-youth.md) — 3-on-3 team drill teaching jump switching, hedge-and-recover, and trapping options off on-ball screens — with help-side rotation responsibilities for the third defender [S15, pp.291-293]
- [Drill draw the charge youth](drill-draw-the-charge-youth.md) — Individual/team drill teaching the help-side defender to slide from proper flat-triangle positioning into a charge-drawing position before the driver leaves the floor for a layup [S15, pp.294-295]
- [Drill help and recover youth](drill-help-and-recover-youth.md) — Individual help-side drill: weak-side defender hedges toward a driver, recovers to assignment, then closes out live 1-on-1 — teaches hedging vs. rotation decision-making [S15, p.296]
- [Drill rotation youth](drill-rotation-youth) — Rotation drill (#143): 3-on-3 defensive rotation drill — X4 calls hedge/rotate/trap when the ball handler beats X1, training the complete help-side rotation system [S15, pp.297-299].
- [Drill four individual defensive traits](drill-four-individual-defensive-traits.md) — Four Individual Defensive Traits drill (#144): one defender (X1) cycles through 4 sequential phases covering 1-on-1, denial, help-side, and rotation vs 5 offensive players — 10-minute comprehensive defensive gauntlet [S15, pp.300-302].
- [Drill mass wave sliding](drill-mass-wave-sliding.md) — Mass Wave Sliding drill (#145): coach-led mass defensive footwork drill — all players react simultaneously to coach's offensive moves with correct defensive footwork responses [S15, p.304-305].
- [Drill jump to the ball youth](drill-jump-to-the-ball-youth.md) — Jump to the Ball drill (#146): defenders practice moving to proper interception-stance position on every pass, with live progressions to backdoor cuts and help-side rotation [S15, pp.306-307].
- [Drill deny the wing youth](drill-deny-the-wing-youth.md) — Deny the Wing drill (#147): defender X3 uses the fence slide to deny a wing V-cut receiver, with backdoor option and 1-on-1 progression — core man-to-man ball-side denial drill [S15, p.308].
- [Drill deny the flash pivot youth](drill-deny-the-flash-pivot-youth.md) — Deny the Flash Pivot drill (#148): defender body-checks a post player flashing to the high post and uses deny-the-wing techniques to prevent the pass — with backdoor counter and 1-on-1 progression [S15, p.309].
- [Drill dribble closeout youth](drill-dribble-closeout-youth.md) — Dribble Closeout drill (#149): defender closes out on a live dribbler and uses overplay/swing steps to keep them under control — three levels from control dribble to live 1-on-1 [S15, pp.310-311].
- [Drill skip pass closeout youth](drill-skip-pass-closeout-youth.md) — Skip Pass and Closeout drill (#150): defender holds interception stance against line-drive passes then closes out on the lob skip pass — with V-cut repositioning and live 1-on-1 [S15, pp.312-313].
- [Drill eight point defensive drill](drill-eight-point-defensive-drill.md) — Eight-Point Drill (#151): advanced 8-part individual defense gauntlet covering 4 strong-side and 4 weak-side scenarios — jump to ball, post defense, corner denial, closeout, interception, flash pivot denial, and 1-on-1 [S15, pp.314-315].
- [Drill one on one multiple skills](drill-one-on-one-multiple-skills.md) — One-on-One Multiple Skills Drill (#152): comprehensive 3-figure defensive drill teaching all help-side, post defense, and weak-side mechanics in one extended sequence — late-season individual defense check-up [S15, pp.316+].
- [Drill s15 shell drill](drill-s15-shell-drill.md) — 10-part youth shell drill (4-on-4 half court) teaching jump-to-ball, deny, closeout, rotation, flash defense, screen defense, and post defense for beginner through advanced players [S15, pp.320-321].
- [Drill s15 five on five](drill-s15-five-on-five.md) — 5-on-5 full team scrimmage format with adjustable rules for motion offense and defense — the culminating team drill of the youth defensive system, with five competitive option variations [S15, p.322].
- [Drill s15 run and jump](drill-s15-run-and-jump.md) — Run-and-jump defensive stunt drill (two-player and three-player variations plus hedge-and-recover) that forces turnovers from dribble penetrators at half court — for intermediate-level youth teams [S15, pp.324-325].
- [Drill s15 run and trap](drill-s15-run-and-trap.md) — Run-and-trap defensive stunt drill from a 1-3-1 formation — two trappers hold the dribbler while three teammates cover passing lanes using safety or all-out interception techniques [S15, pp.326-327].
- [Drill s15 trap the dribble](drill-s15-trap-the-dribble.md) — Youth 'Trap the Dribble' drill — X1 channels the dribbler into a midcourt direction change, signaling X3 to arrive and set a two-man trap; remaining defenders play safety or all-out interception [S15, pp.328-329].
- [Drill s15 trap the pass](drill-s15-trap-the-pass.md) — Youth 'Trap the Pass' drill — X3 deliberately opens the passing lane to the wing to invite a pass, then X1 and X3 immediately trap the receiver; remaining defenders use safety or all-out interception coverage [S15, pp.330-331].
- [Drill s15 channeling](drill-s15-channeling.md) — Youth 'Channeling' drill — defender fans or funnels the dribbler in a pre-determined direction using shuffle-steps and positioning to set up traps; both fanning and funneling are drilled [S15, pp.332-333].
- [Drill s15 zigzag with trapper](drill-s15-zigzag-with-trapper.md) — Youth 'Zigzag With a Trapper' drill — progressive 1v1 channeling drill that adds a second defender (trapper) who arrives on direction changes, teaching dribbling counters and trapping simultaneously [S15, pp.334-335].
- [Drill interval training basketball](drill-interval-training-basketball.md) — Lee Rose's 10-day preseason interval training program — position-graded 200m and 400m intervals with clock-based accountability for guards, forwards, and centers [S13, pp.3-5].
- [Drill basketball sit up](drill-basketball-sit-up.md) — Partner-assisted sit-up for basketball preseason — core strength builder in the agility/power station circuit, 45 seconds per set [S13, p.6].
- [Drill six basket free throws](drill-six-basket-free-throws.md) — Six-Basket Free Throws — competitive consecutive-makes FT drill for teams with multiple baskets; pairs incentive/penalty with individual accountability.
- [Drill two basket free throws](drill-two-basket-free-throws.md) — Two-Basket Free Throws — three variations of competitive FT drills for teams with only two baskets, including split-group, consecutive-make, and team-progression formats.
- [Drill three point shooting competitive](drill-three-point-shooting-competitive.md) — Competitive three-point shooting team drill — three teams compete to make 5 or 10 shots from one of five key spots; winner stays, loser rotates out.
- [Drill make em to move](drill-make-em-to-move.md) — Make 'Em to Move — three-team three-point shooting drill where each player must make one three-pointer before the team rotates to the next of five spots; first to complete all five spots wins.
- [Drill ucla movement](drill-ucla-movement.md) — UCLA Movement 3-on-3 drill: teaches floor balance, spacing, screening, and timing with a 5-pass-before-shooting rule — foundational for the LA Offense [S13, p.132].
- [Drill guard to forward pattern](drill-guard-to-forward-pattern.md) — LA Offense Guard-to-Forward Pass Pattern drill: 5-player half-court sequence with 3 continuity options including ball reversal, stagger screen, and PnR [S13, pp.133-134].
- [Drill guard to guard pattern](drill-guard-to-guard-pattern.md) — LA Offense Guard-to-Guard Pass Pattern drill: position exchange, back screen, weak-side pin-down, and PnR options from a two-guard front [S13, pp.135-136].
- [Drill guard to center pattern](drill-guard-to-center-pattern.md) — LA Offense Guard-to-Center Pass Pattern drill: high-post entry with automatic backdoor cut, guard-around, double-stack screen options, and three releases [S13, pp.136-137].
- [Drill defending cross screens](drill-defending-cross-screens.md) — 5-on-5 half-court drill teaching cross screen defense — X1 bumps the screener, X5 pushes the cutter baseline, and XI steps into the passing lane [S13, pp.207-208].
- [Drill defending sideline pnr](drill-defending-sideline-pnr.md) — 5-on-5 half-court drill defending the sideline pick-and-roll — predetermined technique at the point of the screen, rotation on the trap, and rotation rules for all five defenders [S13, pp.211-212].
- [Drill defending middle pnr](drill-defending-middle-pnr.md) — 5-on-5 half-court drill defending the middle pick-and-roll — soft coverage, no-split rule, and managing the high-low threat when the screener rolls and the second big pops [S13, pp.212-213].
- [Drill defending drag sets](drill-defending-drag-sets.md) — Transition PnR (drag set) defense drill off a made free throw — backcourt sideline coverage, communication when screened in transition, and the X5 switch-and-string-out rule [S13, pp.214-215].
- [Exercise power clean basketball](exercise-power-clean-basketball.md) — Power clean from the floor — the foundational Olympic lift for basketball total-body explosive power, with full technique, breathing, coaching cues, and the lateral clean variation [S11, pp.8-10].
- [Exercise hang clean basketball](exercise-hang-clean-basketball.md) — Hang clean — barbell Olympic lift from above-knee position simulating the athletic/vertical jump stance, for basketball explosive power development [S11, pp.11-12].
- [Exercise power snatch basketball](exercise-power-snatch-basketball.md) — Power snatch from the floor — wide-grip Olympic lift developing total-body explosive power and overhead shoulder stability for basketball [S11, pp.13-15].
- [Exercise one arm dumbbell snatch](exercise-one-arm-dumbbell-snatch.md) — One-arm dumbbell snatch — unilateral Olympic lift variation developing basketball-specific single-arm explosive power and mimicking the unilateral demands of on-court movement [S11, pp.16-17].
- [Exercise hang snatch basketball](exercise-hang-snatch-basketball.md) — Hang snatch — wide-grip Olympic lift from above-knee position developing total-body explosive power and overhead stability for basketball [S11, pp.18-19].
- [Exercise hang pull basketball](exercise-hang-pull-basketball.md) — Hang pull — explosive barbell pull from above-knee position to chest height; the most accessible Olympic-family exercise for basketball, requiring no catch and developing the same explosive triple-extension power [S11, pp.20].
- [Exercise cable squat to row](exercise-cable-squat-to-row.md) — Cable squat to row — compound lower + upper body exercise combining a bilateral squat with a cable row, targeting glutes, hamstrings, quads, and upper back simultaneously [S11, Ch.6]
- [Exercise isometric mid thigh pull](exercise-isometric-mid-thigh-pull.md) — Isometric mid-thigh pull — rack-based maximal isometric pull for assessing and developing peak lower-body force production in basketball athletes [S11, Ch.6]
- [Exercise back squat nsca](exercise-back-squat-nsca.md) — Back squat complete technique guide from NSCA basketball strength training — high/low bar positions, two-spotter protocol, box squat and Hatfield squat variations [S11, Ch.6]
- [Exercise front squat nsca](exercise-front-squat-nsca.md) — Front squat complete technique guide — crossed-arm and parallel-arm bar positions, two-spotter protocol, goblet squat variation, with basketball-specific application [S11, Ch.6]
- [Exercise deadlift nsca](exercise-deadlift-nsca.md) — Deadlift complete technique guide from NSCA basketball strength training — starting position, movement phases, breathing, and coaching tips for basketball-specific posterior chain development [S11, Ch.6]
- [Exercise barbell hip thrust nsca](exercise-barbell-hip-thrust-nsca.md) — Barbell hip thrust complete technique guide — bench-supported glute-dominant hip extension exercise for basketball jumping, sprinting, and horizontal force production [S11, Ch.6]
- [Exercise romanian deadlift nsca](exercise-romanian-deadlift-nsca.md) — Romanian deadlift complete technique guide from NSCA basketball — hip hinge from standing, hamstring/glute focus, coaching cues, and dumbbell/kettlebell variation [S11, Ch.6]
- [Drill hamstring slide](drill-hamstring-slide.md) — Hamstring slide on a slide board — supine bridge position with heels on the board, slide out and curl back — builds posterior chain strength for basketball jumping and deceleration.
- [Drill barbell jump squat](drill-barbell-jump-squat.md) — Barbell jump squat — countermovement quarter-squat into a maximal vertical jump with a bar on the back; develops rate of force development and explosive lower-body power for basketball.
- [Drill glute ham raise](drill-glute-ham-raise.md) — Glute-ham raise on a specialized bench — knee flexion against gravity while maintaining hip extension — elite posterior chain developer for basketball hamstrings, glutes, and spinal erectors.
- [Drill nordic hamstring curl](drill-nordic-hamstring-curl.md) — Nordic hamstring curl — eccentric hamstring exercise from kneeling position, lowering the torso as slowly as possible and catching with hands — elite injury prevention and posterior chain builder for basketball.
- [Drill forward step lunge](drill-forward-step-lunge.md) — Barbell forward step lunge — bilateral lower-body strength exercise stepping forward into a lunge position and returning — develops quad, glute, and hamstring strength for basketball acceleration and jumping.
- [Drill walking lunge](drill-walking-lunge.md) — Walking lunge with dumbbells — continuous forward-stepping lunge pattern (push through to the next step rather than returning) — builds lower body strength, dynamic balance, and hip flexor strength for basketball.
- [Drill side lunge](drill-side-lunge.md) — Side lunge with dumbbells or kettlebell — lateral step with single-leg squat on the lead leg while trailing leg stays straight — builds hip abductors/adductors and lateral strength essential for basketball cuts and defensive slides.
- [Drill pistol squat](drill-pistol-squat.md) — Pistol squat — single-leg squat on the edge of a plyometric box with the opposite leg suspended — develops unilateral lower-body strength, balance, and proprioception for basketball cutting and contact stability.
- [Drill single leg romanian deadlift](drill-single-leg-romanian-deadlift.md) — Single-leg Romanian deadlift with a kettlebell — unilateral hip hinge developing hamstrings, glutes, and spinal erectors for basketball balance, deceleration, and injury prevention.
- [Exercise bulgarian split squat](exercise-bulgarian-split-squat.md) — Bulgarian split squat (rear-foot elevated single-leg squat) — primary unilateral leg strength exercise for basketball, targeting glutes, hamstrings, and quads with barbell, dumbbell, or kettlebell.
- [Exercise step up](exercise-step-up.md) — Step-up exercise — barbell or dumbbell unilateral leg strength drill building glutes, hamstrings, and quads for basketball jumping and acceleration.
- [Exercise drop step squat](exercise-drop-step-squat.md) — Drop step squat — lateral hip abduction into a sumo squat stance, building hip abductor and posterior chain strength for defensive slides and defensive position changes.
- [Exercise single leg cable hip abduction](exercise-single-leg-cable-hip-abduction.md) — Single-leg cable hip abduction — isolation exercise for gluteus medius, gluteus minimus, and TFL, building lateral hip strength critical for defensive slides and direction changes.
- [Exercise dumbbell bench press](exercise-dumbbell-bench-press.md) — Dumbbell bench press for basketball — primary upper-body pushing exercise building pectoralis major, anterior deltoid, and triceps strength for post play, passing, and contact resistance.
- [Exercise one arm cable chest press](exercise-one-arm-cable-chest-press.md) — One-arm cable chest press — unilateral standing pressing exercise building chest, shoulder, and core stability for basketball passing, shooting, and contact resistance.
- [Exercise one arm cable row](exercise-one-arm-cable-row.md) — One-arm cable row — unilateral standing pulling exercise building latissimus dorsi, trapezius, rhomboids, and posterior deltoid strength for basketball rebounding and defensive physicality.
- [Exercise lat pulldown machine](exercise-lat-pulldown-machine.md) — Lat pulldown (machine) — seated bilateral upper-back pulling exercise building latissimus dorsi, trapezius, and posterior deltoid strength for basketball rebounding, running posture, and overhead actions.
- [Exercise pull up basketball](exercise-pull-up-basketball.md) — Pull-up for basketball — complete technique, spotting, grip variations, and coaching cues for upper-back strength development [S11].
- [Exercise bent over row basketball](exercise-bent-over-row-basketball.md) — Barbell bent-over row for basketball — hip-hinge setup, pronated grip, torso-parallel pull to lower chest, with dumbbell and supinated variations [S11].
- [Exercise face pull basketball](exercise-face-pull-basketball.md) — Face pull — high-pulley cable exercise building posterior deltoid, trapezius, and rhomboid strength for shoulder health in basketball [S11].
- [Exercise lateral shoulder raise](exercise-lateral-shoulder-raise.md) — Lateral shoulder raise — dumbbell deltoid exercise building medial shoulder strength for overhead actions, rebounding, and shot-blocking in basketball [S11].
- [Exercise plate front shoulder raise](exercise-plate-front-shoulder-raise.md) — Plate front shoulder raise — anterior deltoid exercise with a weight plate raised to shoulder height, building front-shoulder strength for basketball passing and shooting [S11].
- [Exercise standing dumbbell shoulder press](exercise-standing-dumbbell-shoulder-press.md) — Standing dumbbell shoulder press — bilateral overhead pressing exercise for deltoid and triceps strength; basketball applications for shooting, rebounding, and blocking [S11].
- [Exercise prone yti basketball](exercise-prone-yti-basketball.md) — Prone Y's, T's, I's — three-position scapular stabilizer and rotator cuff strengthening series on incline bench or stability ball for basketball shoulder health [S11].
- [Exercise triceps pushdown](exercise-triceps-pushdown.md) — Triceps pushdown (cable machine) — isolated triceps brachii exercise for elbow extension strength; basketball applications for passing power and shot-blocking [S11].
- [Exercise barbell biceps curl](exercise-barbell-biceps-curl.md) — Barbell biceps curl for basketball — supinated grip elbow flexion exercise building arm strength for rebounding, driving, and ball security [S11].
- [Exercise dumbbell biceps curl](exercise-dumbbell-biceps-curl.md) — Dumbbell biceps curl with supination — unilateral alternating arm curl that develops bilateral biceps strength and forearm supination power for basketball [S11].
- [Exercise bicep curl basketball](exercise-bicep-curl-basketball.md) — Barbell/dumbbell bicep curl for basketball — elbow flexion strength for ball security, rebounding, and body control — with hammer and cable variations [S11].
